          List of busiest airports\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a class="mw-redirect" style="border:none;padding:0">\n          <div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">\n           Related topics\n          </div>\n          <div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n           <ul>\n            <li>\n             <center>\n              <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Central_America-related_articles" title="Index of Central America-related articles">\n               Index of articles\n              </a>\n             </center>\n <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone" title="Central Time Zone">\n              Central Time Zone\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:Central_America_series" title="Template:Central America series">\n             <abbr title="View this template">\n              v\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Central_America_series" title="Template talk:Central America series">\n             <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n              t\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Central_America_series&amp;action=edit">\n             <abbr title="Edit this template">\n              e\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Central America\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n        <i>\n         Am\xc3\xa9rica Central\n        </i>\n        or\n        <i>\n         Centroam\xc3\xa9rica\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ) is the southernmost,\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">\n        isthmian\n       </a>\n       portion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North American\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">\n        continent\n       </a>\n       , which connects with the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South American\n       </a>\n       continent on the southeast. Central America is bordered by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       to the north,\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Colombia\n       </a>\n       to the southeast, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">\n        Caribbean Sea\n       </a>\n       to the east, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">\n        Pacific Ocean\n       </a>\n       to the west. Central America consists of seven countries:\n       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">\n        Belize\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">\n        Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">\n        El Salvador\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">\n        Guatemala\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">\n        Honduras\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">\n        Nicaragua\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">\n        Panama\n       </a>\n       . The combined population of Central America is between 41,739,000 (2009 estimate)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook2013_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handbook2013-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 42,688,190 (2012 estimate).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndexMundi2012_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IndexMundi2012-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Central America is a part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">\n        Mesoamerican\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">\n        biodiversity hotspot\n       </a>\n       , which extends from northern Guatemala through to central Panama. Due to the presence of several\n       <a href="/wiki/Active_fault" title="Active fault">\n        active geologic faults\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_America_Volcanic_Arc" title="Central America Volcanic Arc">\n        Central America Volcanic Arc\n       </a>\n       , there is a great deal of seismic activity in the region.\n       <a href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruptions" title="Types of volcanic eruptions">\n        Volcanic eruptions\n       </a>\n       and earthquakes occur frequently; these natural disasters have resulted in the loss of many lives and much property.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">\n        Pre-Columbian era\n       </a>\n       , Central America was inhabited by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">\n        indigenous\n       </a>\n       peoples of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">\n        Mesoamerica\n       </a>\n       to the north and west and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmo-Colombian_Area" title="Isthmo-Colombian Area">\n        Isthmo-Colombian\n       </a>\n       peoples to the south and east. Soon after\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">\n        Christopher Columbus\n       </a>\n       \'s voyages to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">\n        Americas\n       </a>\n       , the Spanish began to\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">\n        colonize the Americas\n       </a>\n       . From 1609 until 1821, most of the territory within Central America\xe2\x80\x94except for the lands that would become Belize and Panama\xe2\x80\x94was governed by the Viceroyalty of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">\n        New Spain\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">\n        Mexico City\n       </a>\n       as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">\n        Captaincy General of Guatemala\n       </a>\n       . After New Spain achieved independence from Spain in 1821, some of its provinces were annexed to the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">\n        First Mexican Empire\n       </a>\n       , but soon seceded from Mexico to form the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">\n        Federal Republic of Central America\n       </a>\n       , which lasted from 1823 to 1838. The seven states finally became independent autonomous states: beginning with Nicaragua, Honduras, Costa Rica, and Guatemala (1838); followed by El Salvador (1841); then Panama (1903); and finally Belize (1981). Even today, though, people in Central America sometimes still refer to their nations as though they are provinces of a Central American state (e.g. it is still common to write "C.A." after the country names, in formal and informal contexts).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n 8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Politics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a   </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span     <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Different_definitions">\n        Different definitions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Different definitions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       "Central America" may mean different things to various people, based upon different contexts:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_the_Americas" title="United Nations geoscheme for the Americas">\n         United Nations geoscheme for the Americas\n        </a>\n        defines the region as all states of mainland North America south of the United States and specifically includes all of Mexico.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2013_4-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-UN2013-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_(Americas)" title="Middle America (Americas)">\n         Middle America\n        </a>\n        is usually thought to comprise\n        <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n         Mexico\n        </a>\n        to the north of the 7 states of\n        <i>\n         Central America\n        </i>\n        as well as\n        <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n         Colombia\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n         Venezuela\n        </a>\n        to the south. Usually the whole of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">\n         Caribbean\n        </a>\n        to the north-east and sometimes the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guyanas" title="Guyanas">\n         Guyanas\n        </a>\n        are also included.\n        <br/>\n        According to one source, the term "Central America" was used as a synonym for "\n        <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_(Americas)" title="Middle America (Americas)">\n         Middle America\n        </a>\n        " at least as recently as 1962.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Augelli1962_5-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Augelli1962-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In\n        <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">\n         Ibero-America\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">\n         Latin America\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">\n         Iberia\n        </a>\n        ), the\n        <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">\n         Americas\n        </a>\n        is considered a single continent, and Central America is considered a\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">\n         subcontinent\n        </a>\n        separate from\n        <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n         North America\n        </a>\n        comprising the seven countries south of Mexico and north of Colombia.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n         <a href="#cite_note-6">\n          [6]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In Brazil, Central America comprises all countries between Mexico and Colombia, including those in the Caribbean.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Mexico, in whole or in part, is sometimes included by British people.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MW_7-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-MW-7">\n          [7]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burchfield2004_8-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Burchfield2004-8">\n          [8]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMF2014_9-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-IMF2014-9">\n          [9]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n           <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2016)">\n            not in citation given\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n         <a href="#cite_note-10">\n          [10]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        For the people living in the five countries formerly part of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">\n         Federal Republic of Central America\n        </a>\n        there is a distinction between the Spanish language terms "Am\xc3\xa9rica Central" and "Centroam\xc3\xa9rica". While both can be translated into English as "Central America", "Am\xc3\xa9rica Central" is generally used to refer to the geographical area of the seven countries between\n        <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n         Mexico\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n         Colombia\n        </a>\n        , while "Centroam\xc3\xa9rica" is used when referring to the former members of the Federation emphasizing the shared culture and history of the region.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_America" title="History of Central America">\n        History of Central America\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1798_Cassini_Map_of_Florida,_Louisiana,_Cuba,_and_Central_America_-_Geographicus_-_MessicoFlorida-cassini-1798.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5446" data-file-width="4000" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/1798_Cassini_Map_of_Florida%2C_Louisiana%2C_Cuba%2C_and_Central_America_-_Geographicus_-_MessicoFlorida-cassini-1798.jpg/220px-1798_Cassini_Map_of_Florida%2C_Louisiana%2C_Cuba%2C_and_Central_America_-_Geographicus_-_MessicoFlorida-cassini-1798.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/1798_Cassini_Map_of_Florida%2C_Louisiana%2C_Cuba%2C_and_Central_America_-_Geographicus_-_MessicoFlorida-cassini-1798.jpg/330px-1798_Cassini_Map_of_Florida%2C_Louisiana%2C_Cuba%2C_and_Central_America_-_Geographicus_-_MessicoFlorida-cassini-1798.jpg America, 1798\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tikal_Temple1_2006_08_11.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="293" class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tikal_Temple1_2006_08_11.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tikal" title="Tikal">\n          Tikal\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">\n          Guatemala\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tazumal_10.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1386" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Tazumal_10.jpg/330px-Tazumal_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Tazumal_10.jpg/440px-Tazumal_10.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tazumal_10.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tazumal" title="Tazumal">\n          Tazumal\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">\n          El Salvador\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1662" data-file-width="2357" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg/220px-CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg/330px-CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg/440px-CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CPN_WEST_COURT_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copan" title="Copan">\n          Copan\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">\n          Honduras\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="1024" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg/220px-Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg/330px-Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg/440px-Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altun_Ha_Belize.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Altun_Ha" title="Altun Ha">\n          Altun Ha\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">\n          Belize\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg/220px-Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg/330px-Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg/440px-Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica._Museo_Nacional.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Stone_spheres_of_Costa_Rica" title="Stone spheres of Costa Rica">\n          Stone spheres of Costa Rica\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="771" data-file-width="1080" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/220px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/330px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/440px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ancient_footprints_of_Acahualinca" title="Ancient footprints of Acahualinca">\n          Ancient footprints of Acahualinca\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">\n          Nicaragua\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">\n        Pre-Columbian era\n       </a>\n       , the northern areas of Central America were inhabited by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">\n        indigenous\n       </a>\n       peoples of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">\n        Mesoamerica\n       </a>\n       . Most notable among these were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">\n        Mayans\n       </a>\n       , who had built numerous cities throughout the region, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">\n        Aztecs\n       </a>\n       , who had created a vast empire. The pre-Columbian cultures of eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">\n        El Salvador\n       </a>\n       , eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">\n        Honduras\n       </a>\n       , Caribbean\n       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">\n        Nicaragua\n       </a>\n       , most of\n       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">\n        Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">\n        Panama\n       </a>\n       were predominantly speakers of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chibchan_languages" title="Chibchan languages">\n        Chibchan languages\n       </a>\n       at the time of European contact and are considered by some\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoopes.26Fonseca2003_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hoopes.26Fonseca2003-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       culturally different and grouped in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmo-Colombian_Area" title="Isthmo-Colombian Area">\n        Isthmo-Colombian Area\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">\n        Christopher Columbus\n       </a>\n       \'s voyages to the Americas, the Spanish sent many expeditions to the region, and they began their conquest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">\n        Maya territory\n       </a>\n       in 1523. Soon after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">\n        conquest of the Aztec Empire\n       </a>\n       , Spanish\n       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">\n        conquistador\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alvarado" title="Pedro de Alvarado">\n        Pedro de Alvarado\n       </a>\n       commenced the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Guatemala" title="Spanish conquest of Guatemala">\n        conquest of northern Central America\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">\n        Spanish Empire\n       </a>\n       . Beginning with his arrival in\n       <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">\n        Soconusco\n       </a>\n       in 1523, Alvarado\'s forces systematically conquered and subjugated most of the major Maya kingdoms, including the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%27iche%27_Kingdom_of_Q%27umarkaj" title="K\'iche\' Kingdom of Q\'umarkaj">\n        K\'iche\'\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tz%27utujil_people" title="Tz\'utujil people">\n        Tz\'utujil\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">\n        Pipil\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kaqchikel_people" title="Kaqchikel people">\n        Kaqchikel\n       </a>\n       . By 1528, the conquest of Guatemala was nearly complete, with only the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pet%C3%A9n_Basin" title="Pet\xc3\xa9n Basin">\n        Pet\xc3\xa9n Basin\n       </a>\n       remaining outside the Spanish sphere of influence. The last independent Maya kingdoms \xe2\x80\x93 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kowoj" title="Kowoj">\n        Kowoj\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Itza_people" title="Itza people">\n        Itza people\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 were finally defeated in 1697, as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Pet%C3%A9n" title="Spanish conquest of Pet\xc3\xa9n">\n        Spanish conquest of Pet\xc3\xa9n\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1538, Spain established the\n       <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Panama#First_installation" title="Real Audiencia of Panama">\n        Real Audiencia of Panama\n       </a>\n       , which had jurisdiction over all land from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">\n        Strait of Magellan\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">\n        Gulf of Fonseca\n       </a>\n       . This entity was dissolved in 1543, and most of the territory within Central America then fell under the jurisdiction of the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Guatemala" title="Real Audiencia of Guatemala">\n         Audiencia Real de Guatemala\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . This area included the current territories of Costa Rica, El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, Nicaragua, and the Mexican state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">\n        Chiapas\n       </a>\n       , but excluded the lands that would become Belize and Panama. The president of the Audiencia, which had its seat in\n       <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Guatemala" title="Antigua Guatemala">\n        Antigua Guatemala\n       </a>\n       , was the governor of the entire area. In 1609 the area became a\n       <a href="/wiki/Captaincies_of_the_Spanish_Empire" title="Captaincies of the Spanish Empire">\n        captaincy general\n       </a>\n       and the governor was also granted the title of captain general. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">\n        Captaincy General of Guatemala\n       </a>\n       encompassed most of Central America, with the exception of\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">\n        present-day Belize\n       </a>\n       and Panama.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Captaincy General of Guatemala lasted for more than two centuries, but began to fray after a\n       <a href="/wiki/1811_Independence_Movement" title="1811 Independence Movement">\n        rebellion in 1811\n       </a>\n       which began in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intendant#Spain_and_the_Spanish_Empire" title="Intendant">\n        intendancy\n       </a>\n       of San Salvador. The Captaincy General formally ended on 15 September 1821, with the signing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Central_America" title="Act of Independence of Central America">\n        Act of Independence of Central America\n       </a>\n       . Mexican independence was achieved at virtually the same time with the signing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Treaty of C\xc3\xb3rdoba">\n        Treaty of C\xc3\xb3rdoba\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Mexican_Empire" title="Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire">\n        Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire\n       </a>\n       , and the entire region was finally independent from Spanish authority by 28 September 1821.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From its independence from Spain in 1821 until 1823, the former Captaincy General remained intact as part of the short-lived\n       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">\n        First Mexican Empire\n       </a>\n       . When the\n       <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agust\xc3\xadn de Iturbide">\n        Emperor of Mexico\n       </a>\n       abdicated on 19 March 1823, Central America again became independent. On 1 July 1823, the Congress of Central America peacefully seceded from Mexico and declared absolute independence from all foreign nations, and the region formed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">\n        Federal Republic of Central America\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Federal Republic of Central America was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">\n        representative democracy\n       </a>\n       with its capital at\n       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">\n        Guatemala City\n       </a>\n       . This union consisted of the provinces of Costa Rica, El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras,\n       <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos,_Central_America" title="Los Altos, Central America">\n        Los Altos\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">\n        Mosquito Coast\n       </a>\n       , and Nicaragua. The lowlands of southwest Chiapas, including Soconusco, initially belonged to the Republic until 1824, when Mexico annexed most of Chiapas and began its claims to Soconusco. The Republic lasted from 1823 to 1838, when it disintegrated as a result of civil wars.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The territory that now makes up Belize was heavily contested in a dispute that continued for decades after Guatemala achieved independence (see\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belize_(1506%E2%80%931862)" title="History of Belize (1506\xe2\x80\x931862)">\n        History of Belize (1506\xe2\x80\x931862)\n       </a>\n       . Spain, and later Guatemala, considered this land a\n       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Guatemala" title="Departments of Guatemala">\n        Guatemalan department\n       </a>\n       . In 1862, Britain formally declared it a British colony and named it\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">\n        British Honduras\n       </a>\n       . It became independent as Belize in 1981.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Panama, situated in the southernmost part of Central America on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">\n        Isthmus of Panama\n       </a>\n       , has for most of its history been culturally linked to South America. Panama was part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Tierra_Firme" title="Province of Tierra Firme">\n        Province of Tierra Firme\n       </a>\n       from 1510 until 1538 when it came under the jurisdiction of the newly formed\n       <i>\n        Audiencia Real de Panama\n       </i>\n       . Beginning in 1543, Panama was administered as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">\n        Viceroyalty of Peru\n       </a>\n       , along with all other Spanish possessions in South America. Panama remained as part of the Viceroyalty of Peru until 1739, when it was transferred to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">\n        Viceroyalty of New Granada\n       </a>\n       , the capital of which was located at\n       <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot\xc3\xa1">\n        Santa F\xc3\xa9 de Bogot\xc3\xa1\n       </a>\n       . Panama remained as part of the Viceroyalty of New Granada until the disestablishment of that viceroyalty in 1819. A series of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar%27s_campaign_to_liberate_New_Granada" title="Bol\xc3\xadvar\'s campaign to liberate New Granada">\n        military and political struggles\n       </a>\n       took place from that time until 1822, the result of which produced the republic of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">\n        Gran Colombia\n       </a>\n       . After the dissolution of Gran Colombia in 1830, Panama became part of a successor state, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_New_Granada" title="Republic of New Granada">\n        Republic of New Granada\n       </a>\n       . From 1855 until 1886, Panama existed as\n       <a href="/wiki/Panama_State" title="Panama State">\n        Panama State\n       </a>\n       , first within the Republic of New Granada, then within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Granadine_Confederation" title="Granadine Confederation">\n        Granadine Confederation\n       </a>\n       , and finally within the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Colombia" title="United States of Colombia">\n        United States of Colombia\n       </a>\n       . The United States of Colombia was replaced by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Republic of Colombia\n       </a>\n       in 1886. As part of the Republic of Colombia, Panama State was abolished and it became the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_Department" title="Isthmus Department">\n        Isthmus Department\n       </a>\n       . Despite the many political reorganizations, Colombia was still deeply plagued by conflict, which eventually led to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_Panama_from_Colombia" title="Separation of Panama from Colombia">\n        secession of Panama\n       </a>\n       on 3 November 1903. Only after that time did some begin to regard Panama as a North or Central American entity.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By the 1930s the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Fruit_Company" title="United Fruit Company">\n        United Fruit Company\n       </a>\n       owned 3.5 million acres of land in Central America and the Caribbean and was the single largest land owner in Guatemala. Such holdings gave it great power over the governments of small countries. That was one of the factors that led to the coining of the phrase\n       <a href="/wiki/Banana_Republic" title="Banana Republic">\n        Banana Republic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After more than two hundred years of social unrest, violent conflict and revolution, Central America today remains in a period of political transformation. Poverty, social injustice and violence are still widespread.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Argueta2011_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Argueta2011-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nicaragua is the second poorest country in the western hemisphere (only\n       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">\n        Haiti\n       </a>\n       is poorer).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ticotimes_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ticotimes-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Belize" title="Geography of Belize">\n        Geography of Belize\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Costa_Rica" title="Geography of Costa Rica">\n        Geography of Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a America\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Central_America.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="605" data-file-width="848" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Map_of_Central_America.png/220px-Map_of_Central_America.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Map_of_Central_America.png/330px-Map_of_Central_America.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Map_of_Central_America.png/440px-Map_of_Central_America.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Central_America.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The seven countries of Central America and their capitals\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Central America is the tapering isthmus of southern North America, with unique and varied geographic features. The Pacific Ocean lies to the southwest, the Caribbean Sea lies to the northeast, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       lies to the north. Some\n       <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">\n        physiographists\n       </a>\n       define the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">\n        Isthmus of Tehuantepec\n       </a>\n       as the northern geographic border of Central America,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MW_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MW-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while others use the northwestern borders of Belize and Guatemala. From there, the Central American land mass extends southeastward to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">\n        Isthmus of Panama\n       </a>\n       , where it connects to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific/Choc%C3%B3_natural_region" title="Pacific/Choc\xc3\xb3 natural region">\n        Pacific Lowlands\n       </a>\n       in northwestern South America.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Of the many mountain ranges within Central America, the longest are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">\n        Sierra Madre de Chiapas\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Isabelia" title="Cordillera Isabelia">\n        Cordillera Isabelia\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Talamanca" title="Cordillera de Talamanca">\n        Cordillera de Talamanca\n       </a>\n       . At 4,220 meters (13,850\xc2\xa0ft),\n       <a href="/wiki/Volc%C3%A1n_Tajumulco" title="Volc\xc3\xa1n Tajumulco">\n        Volc\xc3\xa1n Tajumulco\n       </a>\n       is the highest peak in Central America. Other high points of Central America are as listed in the table below:\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <p>\n        <b>\n         High points in Central America\n        </b>\n       </p>\n  </td>\n         <td>\n          3474\n         </td>\n         <td>\n          <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Talamanca" title="Cordillera de Talamanca">\n           Cordillera de Talamanca\n          </a>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </center>\n      <p>\n       Between the mountain ranges lie fertile valleys that are suitable for the raising of livestock and for the production of coffee, tobacco, beans and other crops. Most of the population of Honduras, Costa Rica and Guatemala lives in valleys.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">\n        Trade winds\n       </a>\n       have a significant effect upon the climate of Central America. Temperatures in Central America are highest just prior to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">\n        summer wet season\n       </a>\n       , and are lowest during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">\n        winter dry season\n       </a>\n       , when trade winds contribute to a cooler climate. The highest temperatures occur in April, due to higher levels of sunlight, lower cloud cover and a decrease in trade winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oliver2005_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Oliver2005-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">\n        Biodiversity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_America_bioregion" title="Central America bioregion">\n        Central America bioregion\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="432" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/220px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg/330px-El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/El_Chorreron%2C_San_Fernando%2C_El_Salvador.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Chorreron,_San_Fernando,_El_Salvador.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         El Chorreron in El Salvador\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Central America is part of the Mesoamerican\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">\n        biodiversity hotspot\n       </a>\n       , boasting 7% of the world\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">\n        biodiversity\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webng_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-webng-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Flyway" title="Pacific Flyway">\n        Pacific Flyway\n       </a>\n       is a major north-south\n       <a href="/wiki/Flyway" title="Flyway">\n        flyway\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">\n        migratory birds\n       </a>\n       in the Americas, extending from\n       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">\n        Alaska\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">\n        Tierra del Fuego\n       </a>\n       . Due to the funnel-like shape of its land mass, migratory birds can be seen in very high concentrations in Central America, especially in the spring and autumn. As a bridge between North America and South America, Central America has many species from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nearctic_ecozone" title="Nearctic ecozone">\n        Nearctic\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotropic_ecozone" title="Neotropic ecozone">\n        Neotropic ecozones\n       </a>\n       . However the southern countries (Costa Rica and Panama) of the region have more biodiversity than the northern countries (Guatemala and Belize), meanwhile the central countries (Honduras, Nicaragua and El Salvador) have the least biodiversity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webng_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-webng-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The table below shows recent statistics:\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <p>\n        <b>\n         Biodiversity in Central America (number of different species of terrestrial vertebrate animals and        </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          133\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          684\n         </td>\n         <td </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          8681\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          9927\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align:left;">\n          <span class="flagicon">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Flag_of_Honduras.svg/23px-Flag_of_Honduras.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Flag_of_Honduras.svg/35px-Flag_of_Honduras.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Flag_of_Honduras.svg/46px-Flag_of_Honduras.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>\n          </span>\n          <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">\n           Honduras\n          </a>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MongabayH_22-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-MongabayH-22">\n            [22]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          101\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          699\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          201\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          213\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          1214\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          5680\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          6894\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align:left;">\n          <span class="flagicon">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>\n          </span>\n          <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">\n           Nicaragua\n          </a>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MongabayN_23-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-MongabayN-23">\n            [23]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          61\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          632\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          181\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          178\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          1052\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          7590\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          8642\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align:left;">\n          <span class="flagicon">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/23px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/35px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/45px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>\n          </span>\n          <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">\n           Panama\n          </a>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MongabayP_24-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-MongabayP-24">\n            [24]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          182\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          904\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          241\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          242\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          1569\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          9915\n         </td>\n         <td style="text-align:center;">\n          11484\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </center>\n      <p>\n       Over 300 species of the region\'s flora and fauna are threatened, 107 of which are classified as critically endangered. The underlying problems are\n       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">\n        deforestation\n       </a>\n       , which is estimated by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FAO" title="FAO">\n        FAO\n       </a>\n       at 1.2% per year in Central America and Mexico combined,\n       <a href="/wiki/Habitat_fragmentation" title="Habitat fragmentation">\n        fragmentation\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">\n        rainforests\n       </a>\n       and the fact that 80% of the vegetation in Central America has already been converted to agriculture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey2008_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Harvey2008-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Efforts to protect fauna and flora in the region are made by creating\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">\n        ecoregions\n       </a>\n       and nature reserves. 36% of Belize\'s land territory falls under some form of official protected status, giving Belize one of the most extensive systems of terrestrial protected areas in the Americas. In addition, 13% of Belize\'s marine territory are also protected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramos2010_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ramos2010-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A large coral reef extends from Mexico to Honduras: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_Barrier_Reef_System" title="Mesoamerican Barrier Reef System">\n        Mesoamerican Barrier Reef System\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Belize_Barrier_Reef" title="Belize Barrier Reef">\n        Belize Barrier Reef\n       </a>\n       is part of this. The Belize Barrier Reef is home to a large diversity of plants and animals, and is one of the most diverse\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystems\n       </a>\n       of the world. It is home to 70 hard coral species, 36\n       <a href="/wiki/Alcyonacea" title="Alcyonacea">\n        soft coral\n       </a>\n       species, 500 species of fish and hundreds of\n       <a href="/wiki/Invertebrate" title="Invertebrate">\n        invertebrate\n       </a>\n       species. So far only about 10% of the species in the Belize barrier reef have been discovered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-westminster_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-westminster-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">\n        Flora\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flora">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg/220px-Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg/330px-Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg/440px-Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Costa_rica_santa_elena_skywalk.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         One of the hanging bridges of the skywalk at the\n         <a href="/wiki/Monteverde_Cloud_Forest_Reserve" title="Monteverde Cloud Forest Reserve">\n          Monteverde Cloud Forest Reserve\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monteverde,_Costa_Rica" title="Monteverde, Costa Rica">\n          Monteverde, Costa Rica\n         </a>\n         disappearing into the clouds\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       From 2001 to 2010, 5,376 square kilometers (2,076\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of forest were lost in the region. In 2010 Belize had 63% of remaining forest cover, Costa Rica 46%, Panama 45%, Honduras 41%, Guatemala 37%, Nicaragua 29%, and El Salvador 21%. Most of the loss occurred in the moist forest\n       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">\n        biome\n       </a>\n       , with 12,201 square kilometers (4,711\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi). Woody vegetation loss was partially set off by a gain in the coniferous forest biome with 4,730 square kilometers (1,830\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi), and a gain in the dry forest biome at 2,054 square kilometers (793\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi). Mangroves and deserts contributed only 1% to the loss in forest vegetation. The bulk of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Central_America" title="Deforestation in Central America">\n        deforestation\n       </a>\n       was located at the Caribbean slopes of Nicaragua with a loss of 8,574 square kilometers (3,310\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of forest in the period from 2001 to 2010. The most significant regrowth of 3,050 square kilometers (1,180\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of forest was seen in the coniferous woody vegetation of Honduras.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redo2012_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Redo2012-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_pine-oak_forests" title="Central American pine-oak forests">\n        Central American pine-oak forests\n       </a>\n       ecoregion, in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_coniferous_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical coniferous forests">\n        tropical and subtropical coniferous forests\n       </a>\n       biome, is found in Central America and southern Mexico. The Central American pine-oak forests occupy an area of 111,400 square kilometers (43,000\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0303_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0303-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       extending along the mountainous spine of Central America, extending from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">\n        Sierra Madre de Chiapas\n       </a>\n       in Mexico\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">\n        Chiapas\n       </a>\n       state through the highlands of Guatemala, El Salvador, and Honduras to central Nicaragua. The pine-oak forests lie between 600\xe2\x80\x931,800 metres (2,000\xe2\x80\x935,900\xc2\xa0ft) elevation,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0303_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0303-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and are surrounded at lower elevations by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_moist_forests" title="Tropical moist forests">\n        tropical moist forests\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_dry_forests" title="Tropical dry forests">\n        tropical dry forests\n       </a>\n       . Higher elevations above 1,800 metres (5,900\xc2\xa0ft) are usually covered with\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_montane_forests" title="Central American montane forests">\n        Central American montane forests\n       </a>\n       . The Central American pine-oak forests are composed of many species characteristic of temperate North America including\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">\n        oak\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">\n        pine\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">\n        fir\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cypress" title="Cypress">\n        cypress\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest" title="Laurel forest">\n        Laurel forest\n       </a>\n       is the most common type of Central American temperate evergreen\n       <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">\n        cloud forest\n       </a>\n       , found in almost all Central American countries, normally more than 1,000 meters (3,300\xc2\xa0ft) above sea level. Tree species include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergreen_oak" title="Evergreen oak">\n        evergreen oaks\n       </a>\n       , members of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Laurus" title="Laurus">\n        laurel family\n       </a>\n       , and species of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Weinmannia" title="Weinmannia">\n         Weinmannia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Drimys" title="Drimys">\n         Drimys\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Magnolia" title="Magnolia">\n         Magnolia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0167_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0167-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The cloud forest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_las_Minas" title="Sierra de las Minas">\n        Sierra de las Minas\n       </a>\n       , Guatemala, is the largest in Central America. In some areas of southeastern Honduras there are cloud forests, the largest located near the border with Nicaragua. In Nicaragua, cloud forests are situated near the border with Honduras, but many were cleared to grow coffee. There are still some temperate evergreen hills in the north. The only cloud forest in the Pacific coastal zone of Central America is on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mombacho" title="Mombacho">\n        Mombacho\n       </a>\n       volcano in Nicaragua. In Costa Rica, there are laurel forests in the Cordillera de\n       <a href="/wiki/Tilar%C3%A1n" title="Tilar\xc3\xa1n">\n        Tilar\xc3\xa1n\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volc%C3%A1n_Arenal" title="Volc\xc3\xa1n Arenal">\n        Volc\xc3\xa1n Arenal\n       </a>\n       , called\n       <a href="/wiki/Monteverde" title="Monteverde">\n        Monteverde\n       </a>\n       , also in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Talamanca" title="Cordillera de Talamanca">\n        Cordillera de Talamanca\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_montane_forests" title="Central American montane forests">\n        Central American montane forests\n       </a>\n       are an ecoregion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">\n        tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests\n       </a>\n       biome, as defined by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">\n        World Wildlife Fund\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0112_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0112-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These forests are of the moist deciduous and the semi-evergreen seasonal subtype of tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests and receive high overall rainfall with a warm summer\n       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">\n        wet season\n       </a>\n       and a cooler winter dry season. Central American montane forests consist of forest patches located at altitudes ranging from 1,800\xe2\x80\x934,000 metres (5,900\xe2\x80\x9313,100\xc2\xa0ft), on the summits and slopes of the highest mountains in Central America ranging from Southern Mexico, through Guatemala, El Salvador, and Honduras, to northern Nicaragua. The entire ecoregion covers an area of 13,200 square kilometers (5,100\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) and has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">\n        temperate climate\n       </a>\n       with relatively high\n       <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">\n        precipitation\n       </a>\n       levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0112_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0112-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">\n        Fauna\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Fauna">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Central_American_mammals" title="List of Central American mammals">\n        List of Central American mammals\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Central_American_monkey_species" title="List of Central American monkey species">\n        List of Central American monkey species\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ecoregions are not only established to protect the forests themselves but also because they are habitats for an incomparably rich and often endemic fauna. Almost half of the bird population of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Talamancan_montane_forests" title="Talamancan montane forests">\n        Talamancan montane forests\n       </a>\n       in Costa Rica and Panama are endemic to this region. Several birds are listed as threatened, most notably the\n       <a href="/wiki/Resplendent_quetzal" title="Resplendent quetzal">\n        resplendent quetzal\n       </a>\n       (Pharomacrus mocinno),\n       <a href="/wiki/Three-wattled_bellbird" title="Three-wattled bellbird">\n        three-wattled bellbird\n       </a>\n       (Procnias tricarunculata),\n       <a href="/wiki/Bare-necked_umbrellabird" title="Bare-necked umbrellabird">\n        bare-necked umbrellabird\n       </a>\n       (Cephalopterus glabricollis), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Black_guan" title="Black guan">\n        black guan\n       </a>\n       (Chamaepetes unicolor). Many of the amphibians are endemic and depend on the existence of forest. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Golden_toad" title="Golden toad">\n        golden toad\n       </a>\n       that once inhabited a small region in the Monteverde Reserve, which is part of the Talamancan montane forests, has not been seen alive since 1989 and is listed as extinct by IUCN. The exact causes for its extincition are unknown. Global warming may have played a role, because the development of fog that is typical for this area may have been compromised. Seven small mammals are endemic to the Costa Rica-Chiriqui highlands within the Talamancan montane forest region.\n       <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">\n        Jaguars\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">\n        cougars\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Spider_monkey" title="Spider monkey">\n        spider monkeys\n       </a>\n       , as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">\n        tapirs\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">\n        anteaters\n       </a>\n       live in the woods of Central America.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF0167_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WWF0167-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_red_brocket" title="Central American red brocket">\n        Central American red brocket\n       </a>\n       is a brocket deer found in Central America\'s tropical forest.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">\n        Geology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/220px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/330px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/440px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Central America and the\n         <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">\n          Caribbean Plate\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_America_Volcanic_Arc" title="Central America Volcanic Arc">\n        Central America Volcanic Arc\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Costa_Rica" title="List of earthquakes in Costa Rica">\n        List of earthquakes in Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_El_Salvador" title="List of earthquakes in El Salvador">\n        List of earthquakes in El Salvador\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Guatemala" title="List of earthquakes in Guatemala">\n        List of earthquakes in Guatemala\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Nicaragua" title="List of earthquakes in Nicaragua">\n        List of earthquakes in Nicaragua\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Central America is geologically very active, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruptions" title="Types of volcanic eruptions">\n        volcanic eruptions\n       </a>\n       and earthquakes occurring frequently, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">\n        tsunamis\n       </a>\n       occurring occasionally. Many thousands of people have died as a result of these natural disasters.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most of Central America rests atop the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">\n        Caribbean Plate\n       </a>\n       . This\n       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">\n        tectonic plate\n       </a>\n       converges with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cocos_Plate" title="Cocos Plate">\n        Cocos\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nazca_Plate" title="Nazca Plate">\n        Nazca\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">\n        North American\n       </a>\n       plates to form the\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_Trench" title="Middle America Trench">\n        Middle America Trench\n       </a>\n       , a major\n       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">\n        subduction zone\n       </a>\n       . The Middle America Trench is situated some 60\xe2\x80\x93160 kilometers (37\xe2\x80\x9399\xc2\xa0mi) off the Pacific coast of Central America and runs roughly parallel to it. Many large earthquakes have occurred as a result of seismic activity at the Middle America Trench.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Astiz1987_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Astiz1987-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, subduction of the Cocos Plate beneath the North American Plate at the Middle America Trench is believed to have caused the\n       <a href="/wiki/1985_Mexico_City_earthquake" title="1985 Mexico City earthquake">\n        1985 Mexico City earthquake\n       </a>\n       that killed as many as 40,000 people. Seismic activity at the Middle America Trench is also responsible for earthquakes in\n       <a href="/wiki/1902_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1902 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1902\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1942_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1942 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1942\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1956_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="1956 Nicaragua earthquake">\n        1956\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1982_El_Salvador_earthquake" title="1982 El Salvador earthquake">\n        1982\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1992_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="1992 Nicaragua earthquake">\n        1992\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_El_Salvador_earthquakes" title="2001 El Salvador earthquakes">\n        2001\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/2007_Guatemala_earthquake" title="2007 Guatemala earthquake">\n        2007\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/2012_Guatemala_earthquake" title="2012 Guatemala earthquake">\n        2012\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/October_2014_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="October 2014 Nicaragua earthquake">\n        2014\n       </a>\n       , and many other earthquakes throughout Central America.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Middle America Trench is not the only source of seismic activity in Central America. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Motagua_Fault" title="Motagua Fault">\n        Motagua Fault\n       </a>\n       is an onshore continuation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Trough" title="Cayman Trough">\n        Cayman Trough\n       </a>\n       which forms part of the tectonic boundary between the North American Plate and the Caribbean Plate. This\n       <a href="/wiki/Transform_fault" title="Transform fault">\n        transform fault\n       </a>\n       cuts right across Guatemala and then continues offshore until it merges with the Middle America Trench along the Pacific coast of Mexico, near\n       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">\n        Acapulco\n       </a>\n       . Seismic activity at the Motagua Fault has been responsible for earthquakes in\n       <a href="/wiki/1717_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1717 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1717\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1773_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1773 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1773\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1902_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1902 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1902\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1976_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1976 Guatemala earthquake">\n        1976\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1980_Honduras_earthquake" title="1980 Honduras earthquake">\n        1980\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/2009_Honduras_earthquake" title="2009 Honduras earthquake">\n        2009\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another onshore continuation of the Cayman Trough is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chixoy-Polochic_Fault" title="Chixoy-Polochic Fault">\n        Chixoy-Polochic Fault\n       </a>\n       , which runs parallel to, and roughly 80 kilometers (50\xc2\xa0mi) to the north, of the Motagua Fault. Though less active than the Motagua Fault, seismic activity at the Chixoy-Polochic Fault is still thought to be capable of producing very large earthquakes, such as the 1816 earthquake of Guatemala.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White1985_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-White1985-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">\n        Managua\n       </a>\n       , the capital of Nicaragua, was devastated by earthquakes in\n       <a href="/wiki/1931_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="1931 Nicaragua earthquake">\n        1931\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/1972_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="1972 Nicaragua earthquake">\n        1972\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Volcanic eruptions are also common in Central America. In 1968 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arenal_Volcano" title="Arenal Volcano">\n        Arenal Volcano\n       </a>\n       , in Costa Rica, erupted killing 87 people as the 3 villages of Tabacon, Pueblo Nuevo and San Luis were buried under pyroclastic flows and debris. Fertile soils from weathered volcanic lava have made it possible to sustain dense populations in the agriculturally productive highland areas.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Central_America" title="Ethnic groups in Central America">\n        Ethnic groups in Central America\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">\n        Latin Americans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The population of Central America is estimated at 47,448,333 as of 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With an area of 523,780 square kilometers (202,230\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook2013_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handbook2013-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       it has a population density of 81 per square kilometer (210/sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">\n       <caption>\n        Countries of Central America\n       </caption>\n
