 </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="462" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png/220px-Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png/330px-Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png/440px-Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Espa%C3%B1ol_centroamericano.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Linguistic variations of classic\n         <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Spanish" title="Central American Spanish">\n          Central American Spanish\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Spanish" title="Central American Spanish">\n        Central American Spanish\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The official language majority in all Central American countries is\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       , except in Belize, where the official language is\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">\n        Mayan languages\n       </a>\n       constitute a\n       <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">\n        language family\n       </a>\n       consisting of about 26 related languages. Guatemala formally recognized 21 of these in 1996.\n       <a href="/wiki/Xincan_languages" title="Xincan languages">\n        Xinca\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_language" title="Garifuna language">\n        Garifuna\n       </a>\n       are also present in Central America.\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <table class="sortable wikitable">\n        <tr>\n       </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centroamerica_prehispanica_siglo_XVI.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="11093" data-file-width="15744" height="155" class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centroamerica_prehispanica_siglo_XVI.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Central America map of indigenous people before European contact\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       This region of the continent is very rich in terms of ethnic groups. The majority of the population is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">\n        mestizo\n       </a>\n       , with sizable Mayan and White populations present, including Xinca and Garifuna minorities. The immigration of Arabs, Jews, Chinese, Europeans and others brought additional groups to the area.\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <table class="wikitable sortable">\n        <tr <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religious groups">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_in_Central_America" title="Anglican Church in Central America">\n        Anglican Church in Central America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Central_America" title="Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith in Central America">\n        Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith in Central America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Central_America" title="Buddhism in Central America">\n        Buddhism in Central America\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_North_America" title="Roman Catholicism in North America">\n        Roman Catholicism in North America\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The predominant religion in Central America is\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">\n        Christianity\n       </a>\n       (95.6%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Beginning with the Spanish colonization of Central America in the 16th century,\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Roman Catholicism\n       </a>\n       became the most popular religion in the region until the first half of the 20th century. Since the 1960s, there has been an increase in other Christian groups, particularly\n       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">\n        Protestantism\n       </a>\n       , as well as other religious organizations, and individuals identifying themselves as having no religion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holland2005_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Holland2005-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="background: Catholicism\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         (2010)\n        </th>\n        <th style="background: #ABCDEF;">\n         %\n         <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">\n          Protestantism\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         (2010)\n        </th>\n        <th style="background: #ABCDEF;">\n         %\n         <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">\n          Non-affiliated\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         (2010)\n        </th>\n        <th style="background: #ABCDEF;">\n         % Other\n         <br/>\n         (2010)\n        </th>\n   </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">\n            Dominican Republic\n           </a>\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n        </table>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Integration_System" title="Central American Integration System">\n        Central American Integration System\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Central America is currently undergoing a process of political, economic and cultural transformation that started in 1907 with the creation of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Court_of_Justice" title="Central American Court of Justice">\n        Central American Court of Justice\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1951 the integration process continued with the signature of the San Salvador Treaty, which created the ODECA, the Organization of Central American States. However, the unity of the ODECA was limited by conflicts between several member states.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1991, the integration agenda was further advanced by the creation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Integration_System" title="Central American Integration System">\n        Central American Integration System\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Sistema para la Integraci\xc3\xb3n Centroamericana\n       </i>\n       , or SICA). SICA provides a clear legal basis to avoid disputes between the member states. SICA membership includes the 7 nations of Central America plus the Dominican Republic, a state that is traditionally considered part of the Caribbean.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 6 December 2008 SICA announced an agreement to pursue a common currency and common passport for the member nations.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       No timeline for implementation was discussed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Central America already has several supranational institutions such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Parliament" title="Central American Parliament">\n        Central American Parliament\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Bank_for_Economic_Integration" title="Central American Bank for Economic Integration">\n        Central American Bank for Economic Integration\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Common_Market" title="Central American Common Market">\n        Central American Common Market\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 22 July 2011 President\n       <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Funes" title="Mauricio Funes">\n        Mauricio Funes\n       </a>\n       of El Salvador became the first president\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pro_tempore" title="Pro tempore">\n         pro tempore\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       to SICA. El Salvador also became the headquarters of SICA with the inauguration of a new building.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BESS2013_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BESS2013-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">\n        Foreign relations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93Latin_America_relations" title="China\xe2\x80\x93Latin America relations">\n        China\xe2\x80\x93Latin America relations\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Until recently, all Central American countries have maintained diplomatic relations with\n       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">\n        Taiwan\n       </a>\n       instead of China. President\n       <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Arias" title="\xc3\x93scar Arias">\n        \xc3\x93scar Arias\n       </a>\n       of Costa Rica, however, established diplomatic relations with China in 2007, severing formal diplomatic ties with Taiwan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCNYT_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TCNYT-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After breaking off relations with the Republic of China in 2017, Panama established diplomatic relations with the People\'s Republic of China.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Central_American_Parliament">\n        Central American Parliament\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Central American Parliament">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2900" data-file-width="4000" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png/220px-Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png/330px-Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png/440px-Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Central_American_Parliament.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flag of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Parliament" title="Central American Parliament">\n          Central American Parliament\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Parliament" title="Central American Parliament">\n        Central American Parliament\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Central American Parliament (also known as PARLACEN) is a political and parliamentary body of SICA. The parliament started around 1980, and its primary goal was to resolve conflicts in Nicaragua, Guatemala, and El Salvador. Although the group was disbanded in 1986, ideas of unity of Central Americans still remained, so a treaty was signed in 1987 to create the Central American Parliament and other political bodies. Its original members were Guatemala, El Salvador, Nicaragua and Honduras. The parliament is the political organ of Central America, and is part of SICA. New members have since then joined including Panama and the Dominican Republic.\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:left;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belize" title="Economy of Belize">\n        Economy of Belize\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Costa_Rica" title="Economy of Costa Rica">\n        Economy of Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_El_Salvador" title="Economy of El Salvador">\n        Economy of El Salvador\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guatemala" title="Economy of Guatemala">\n        Economy of Guatemala\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Honduras" title="Economy of Honduras">\n        Economy of Honduras\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Nicaragua" title="Economy of Nicaragua">\n        Economy of Nicaragua\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Panama" title="Economy of Panama">\n        Economy of Panama\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Signed in 2004, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic%E2%80%93Central_America_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Dominican Republic\xe2\x80\x93Central America Free Trade Agreement">\n        Central American Free Trade Agreement\n       </a>\n       (CAFTA) is an agreement between the United States, Costa Rica, El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, Nicaragua, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">\n        Dominican Republic\n       </a>\n       . The treaty is aimed at promoting\n       <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">\n        free trade\n       </a>\n       among its members.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guatemala has the largest economy in the region.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFWEO2012_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IMFWEO2012-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFGDP2012_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IMFGDP2012-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its main exports are coffee, sugar, bananas, petroleum, clothing, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">\n        cardamom\n       </a>\n       . Of its 10.29 billion dollar annual exports,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciaexport_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ciaexport-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       40.2% go to the United States, 11.1% to neighboring El Salvador, 8% to Honduras, 5.5% to Mexico, 4.7% to Nicaragua, and 4.3% to Costa Rica.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciaexportgu_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ciaexportgu-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Economic growth in Central America is projected to slow slightly in 2014\xe2\x80\x9315, as country-specific domestic factors offset the positive effects from stronger economic activity in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMF2014_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IMF2014-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: 78,012\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align:left;">\n          <span class="flagicon">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500"       </td>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </center>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Belize" title="Tourism in Belize">\n        Tourism in Belize\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Costa_Rica" title="Tourism in Costa Rica">\n        Tourism in Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism_in_Costa_Rica" title="Ecotourism in Costa Rica">\n        Ecotourism in Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nicaragua" title="Tourism in Nicaragua">\n        Tourism in Nicaragua\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Blue_Hole.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="515" data-file-width="662" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Great_Blue_Hole.jpg/220px-Great_Blue_Hole.jpg"         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Blue_Hole.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Great_Blue_Hole" title="Great Blue Hole">\n          Great Blue Hole\n         </a>\n         off the coast of Belize is a prime\n         <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">\n          ecotourism\n         </a>\n         destination. It is a\n         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">\n          UNESCO World Heritage Site\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Semuc_Champey,_Guatemala.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2203" data-file-width="3916" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Semuc_Champey%2C_Guatemala.jpg/220px-Semuc_Champey%2C_Guatemala.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Semuc_Champey%2C_Guatemala.jpg/440px-Semuc_Champey%2C_Guatemala.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Semuc_Champey,_Guatemala.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Semuc_Champey" title="Semuc Champey">\n          Semuc Champey\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">\n          Guatemala\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="3240" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG/220px-Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG/330px-Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG/440px-Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chorros_de_La_Calera.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Chorros de La Calera\n         <a href="/wiki/Juay%C3%BAa" title="Juay\xc3\xbaa">\n          Juay\xc3\xbaa\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">\n          El Salvador\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Belize" title="Tourism in Belize">\n        Tourism in Belize\n       </a>\n       has grown considerably in more recent times, and it is now the second largest industry in the nation. Belizean Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/Dean_Barrow" title="Dean Barrow">\n        Dean Barrow\n       </a>\n       has stated his intention to use tourism to combat poverty throughout the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cuellar2013_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cuellar2013-48">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The growth in tourism has positively affected the agricultural, commercial, and finance industries, as well as the construction industry. The results for Belize\'s tourism-driven economy have been significant, with the nation welcoming almost one million tourists in a calendar year for the first time in its history in 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPS2013_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SPS2013-49">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Belize is also the only country in Central America with English as its official language, making this country a comfortable destination for English-speaking tourists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Costa Rica is the most visited nation in Central America.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodr2014_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rodr2014-51">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Costa_Rica" title="Tourism in Costa Rica">\n        Tourism in Costa Rica\n       </a>\n       is one of the fastest growing economic sectors of the country,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rojas2004_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rojas2004-52">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       having become the largest source of foreign revenue by 1995.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inman1997_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Inman1997-53">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 1999, tourism has earned more foreign exchange than bananas, pineapples and coffee exports combined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitcostarica_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-visitcostarica-54">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The tourism boom began in 1987,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inman1997_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Inman1997-53">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the number of visitors up from 329,000 in 1988, through 1.03 million in 1999, to a historical record of 2.43 million foreign visitors and $1.92-billion in revenue in 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodr2014_51-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rodr2014-51">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012 tourism contributed with 12.5% of the country\'s GDP and it was responsible for 11.7% of direct and indirect employment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wef2013_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wef2013-55">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nicaragua" title="Tourism in Nicaragua">\n        Tourism in Nicaragua\n       </a>\n       has grown considerably recently, and it is now the second largest industry in the nation. Nicaraguan President\n       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">\n        Daniel Ortega\n       </a>\n       has stated his intention to use tourism to combat poverty throughout the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll2007_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carroll2007-56">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The growth in tourism has positively affected the agricultural, commercial, and finance industries, as well as the construction industry. The results for Nicaragua\'s tourism-driven economy have been significant, with the nation welcoming one million tourists in a calendar year for the first time in its history in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sify_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sify-57">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">\n        Transport\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Belize" title="Transport in Belize">\n Panama">\n        Transport in Panama\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">\n        Roads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Roads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Roads_in_Belize" title="Roads in Belize">\n        Roads in Belize\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Highway" title="Inter-American Highway">\n        Inter-American Highway\n       </a>\n       is the Central American section of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">\n        Pan-American Highway\n       </a>\n       , and spans 5,470 kilometers (3,400\xc2\xa0mi) between\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Laredo" title="Nuevo Laredo">\n        Nuevo Laredo, Mexico\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">\n        Panama City, Panama\n       </a>\n       . Because of the 87 kilometers (54\xc2\xa0mi) break in the highway known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dari%C3%A9n_Gap" title="Dari\xc3\xa9n Gap">\n        Dari\xc3\xa9n Gap\n       </a>\n       , it is not possible to cross between Central America and South America in an automobile.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">\n        Waterways\n       </span>\n Retrieved\n            <span class="nowrap">\n             September 4,\n            </span>\n            2016\n           </span>\n           .\n           <q>\n            Central America is located between North and South America and consists of multiple countries. Central America is not a continent but a subcontinent since it lies within the continent America. It borders on the northwest to the Pacific Ocean and in the northeast to the Caribbean Sea. The countries that belong to the subcontinent of Central America are Belize, Costa Rica, El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, Nicaragua and Panama.\n           </q>\n          </cite>\n          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Central+America&amp;rft.pub=central-america.org&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcentral-america.org%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACentral+America">\n           <span style="display:none;">\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-MW-7">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          ^\n          <a href="#cite_ref-MW_7-0">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              a\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-MW_7-1">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              b\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation encyclopaedia">\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.m-w.com/dictionary/Central%20America" rel="nofollow">\n            "Central America"\n           </a>\n           .\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster%27s_Collegiate_Dictionary" title="Merriam-Webster\'s Collegiate Dictionary">\n            Merriam-Webster\'s collegiate dictionary\n           </a>\n           .
